<Content>What a great find! Myself and partner stayed at the Eastgate Towers in Dec 08. Booked at 1 bed suite with Expedia, the cost was less than a small hotel room! The suite was on the 15th floor and had everything (and more) we could have needed. Lovely comfortable massive bed, TV in the lounge and bedroom, full en-suite bathroom and a seperate toilet, full kitchen - although we only used the fridge and dishwasher! The suite was always cleaned, the furniture whilst dated was functional and clean. The service was great one evening requested further pillows these were delievered to suite within 10 minutes, the reception arrange transfers for us back to the airport! There is no restuarant on site but there are so many places to get food this is no problem. We had no problems with the location walked to Grand Central Station in 5/10 mins, Empire State Building was 15 min walk. At the end of a busy day it was nice to get away from the noise and relax in space before going out for the night. Can not wait to go back - loved New York and loved the Eastgate Tower.

<Author>southDublingirl
<Content>A so so stay at the East Gate I have stayed in the Eastgate Tower on a number of ocassions. This trip was for a family holiday. The hotel is in a great location and is wlaking distnace of a lot of attractions. I have to agree with one of the previous reviewrs and say that while the hotel is clean it felt a little grubby and is in need of a major refurb in terms of the decor. We stayed for 10 nights and the while the towels were changed daily the sheets weren't changed at all during our stay. On the first night the sofa bed in one of the rooms we had booked was full of crumbs and had no covers on it. We contacted the housekeeping staff and had to wait four hours for the bed to be made and cleaned so that someone could sleep in it. The noise from the corridor also made it hard to sleep at times. We were located in a room adjacent to what we think was a staff room and the door to this room was closed by a bang throughout the day and night which was quite irritating. The lifts were also slow and hard to get into at peak times.We found the front desk staff to be quite unhelpful. They gave us wrong advise on a number of ocassions. This was in relation to a range of things, for example on new years day they told us all of the major department stores were closed, which was in fact incorrect and theytwere all open. They gave wrong directions and seemed to try to push bus tours and booking these type of things through the front desk. This happened throughout our stay, we were careful to double check any information they gave us.When it came to checking out we found that the service of the front desk staff really failed. It took over an hour and a quarter to check out. One of the rooms was over charged, another was chraged out without telling the person having been told at check in that the credit card was a security thing only and that no chrages would be made until check out and the third rooms money was miss counted by the member of staff who found that they had made a mistake after very reluctantly agreeing to do a recount. The staff member at this point was quite difficult to deal with. It was a very bad way to finish off the stay.Overall I was very disappointed with my stay at the Eastgate. I am a frequent visitor to New York and don't intend to return to the East Gate,. I would also be very reluctant to reccomend it to a friend as we had so many problems. I had organised the stay in this hotel for a large group of family members and was very disappointed with the overall level of service we received.

<Author>stokerej
<Content>Warm welcome at Eastgate We have stayed in many places around the world, but without doubt, the Eastgate offered the warmest greeting ever, despite sub zero termperatures outside. Entrance to the Hotel is via a very small lobby and onwards to the accommodation via 2 smallish lifts. We had a double room which is large by New York standards. The furniture is quite old, although it serves its purpose. There is everything in the kitchen you could want if you wish to make a cup of tea or indeed something more substantial. The kitchen was clean although not pristine and it was the cutlery drawer which I felt needed to be cleaned out. The refuse bins were all emptied on a daily basis. The bathroom/WC was very clean and shower gel, shampoo, conditioner and moisturiser were all provided along with an excellent supply of towels/flannels. I would have no qualms at all in reccommending this hotel but it is ready for some sort of re-furbishment/decoration. The net curtains were really dirty, but as the warm air radiator is directly below the window, this is obviously why the curtains are so dirty. Nevertheless, it is a problem which could so easily be rectified and would make the room much more presentable. The things I have pointed out above in no way detract from the hotel. It would overall, just be so much more appealing. I would stay there again when hopefully some decoration will have taken place and the restaurant which is out of action right now, may well be up and running and should make a big difference to the hotel especially if the prices were competative. Having said that, there is a substantial amount of eateries close by.

<Author>thenutkin
<Content>Good value in an expensive city It is hard to find acceptable accommodations in New York for less than $300 per night. $200 is a steal. So when we secured a junior suite at the Eastgate for less than $150, it was too good an opportunity to pass up.Yes, the decor needs a bit of freshening. I was told that starting in January, the place would be undergoing renovations. Meanwhile, the furniture is serviceable and the space is very generous. All is clean and the beds are triple-sheeted so you won't see the blanket at all. There was a full kitchen and a comfortable seating area with sofa, chair and excellent lighting. We only had a view of another building but that meant there was minimal street noise. Bathroom was small but clean.The location is very convenient for most things. We had to take a train leaving from Grand Central Station which is just a short walk away. There are plenty of restaurants and shopping nearby.Our one peeve was that we could not turn off the heat. Thankfully, the window opened so the fresh air coming in cooled things off to a comfortable temperature.There is virtually no lobby. All the workers we encountered were friendly and helpful. We even parked in the garage in the building. This cost us $34 per 24 hours including all taxes. Not bad for this expensive city.We'll be interested to see how the renovations affect the pricing. Meanwhile, like other Affinia properties that we've tried, this is a well-run establishment.

<Author>DuiDublin
<Content>Fabulous Place - will stay again! It was my first time to NYC for shopping, and I booked the Eastgate Towers a week before I flew out due to a mix up with a previous booking. I was a bit shocked to find that the price was almost half of what I had booked in another hotel only 2 Avenue's down and EastGate Towers was amazing for the price. For the week in NYC I paid only 672 Euros!!! I had an upgrade to a junior suite upon arrival at no extra cost, and the Staff at the front desk were so so very helpful - Morgan did my upgrade. Staff are polite and very helpful - and always able to deliver prompt service when I needed it. I'm a bit of a clean freak when it comes to accom overseas, but I had nothing to complain about during my stay. Some of the floors however are smoking floors so you can smell a bit of it from the stair wells ... but then you're not spending more than a minute in the hallways waiting for the lift so it's no biggie.Around the corner from the hotel is a load of places to eat and drink and Frontiers cafe is serving up the best pancakes I've had in years ... two mornings I had to go back just for the coffee and pancakes ... Dunkin Donuts is a bit further down the street, as is a whole range of other places to grab a bite to eat. There's a NYC Steakhouse about 10 minutes walk from the front door, and also a ton of cocktail bars along the way into Times Sqaure.I've already had a look at my next dates in NYC and the rooms available in May. I'll will certainly be booking another stay there. The rooms are huge, the fridge is massive, the bathrooms are clean.

<Author>AGorthy
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised I was a little fearful of what to expect, this hotel was FAR cheaper than 2.5 star hotels we looked at. I looked at other traveler reviews and concur with what most say. These are very roomy rooms, we stayed in the Junior queen suite, which had a queen bed and a sofa bed. The decor is not great but not bad, I think the room looks better in real life than in the travelers' photos. Our room was comfortable and clean.There is tons of closet space and room to spread out. Our room had one large closet and two smaller closets, one dresser and two nightstands. There was a small kitchen with sink, stove, microwave, toaster, coffee maker and dishes, glassware, silverware and cookware and a table with two chairs. The elevators were reasonably quick for an older building and we had no problems at check-in/check-out.This hotel also had larger suites that could accommodate slightly larger groups of friends. I only had two fairly minor complaints, the location, though not bad, was not really near anything of interest, we were a 15 minute walk to most things, not bad. The other issue is even though the heater said cool and off, it was spewing out hot air and we had not control of this. We had to crack the windows (which is all they would do for safety reasons) and cover the vents with pillows to keep the room at a comfortable level. For the price paid, the space and quality, I would definitely stay here and recommend to others.

<Author>Fuzby
<Content>Good if you need a kitchen I recently visited NYU to give an invited lecture, and my hosts booked me at the Eastgate, which is a convenient place to stay if visiting the NYU medical center, just a few blocks away. The hotel has an odd layout. It is 25 floors tall, but each floor has only 7 rooms, all located within a few feet of the elevators. My room itself was spacious, and had a full kitchen complete with 4-burner stove and oven, pots  pans, microwave, and under the counter refrigerator. There was also plenty of closet and dresser space for the 'extended stay' traveler. But the bathroom was so tiny it was a trick to close the door while in it, and the overall decor was pretty tired. Bed was fine; ancient heating system had two temperatures: Arctic or Amazon Rain Forest. But the noisy fan tended to block out street noise, which was a plus. No food available at the hotel. Overall, I'd pick this for an extended stay, but for a normal business trip it was nothing special.

<Content>We Loved Eastgate Tower Suite Arrived home from a weeks stay about an hour ago and felt compelled to write and sing this Hotel's praises.Had never been to NYC before and neither had my daughters 13 and 17.Spent a good deal of time locating a hotel on the internet and have to say that Tripadvisor swung it for me.Located other seemingly more swanky hotels but this one (I couldnt afford Trump Towers etc.) ticked the boxes and had much better reviews than other more expensive places.We were not disappointed.We had a junior suite which comprises a huge L shaped room with a huge bed my daughters shared and a very comfortable sofa bed that Dad occupied,a dining /writing postcards/quiet area, bathroom with exy shower and kitchenette (we didnt eat in cus eating out is so cheap - we ate out for as little as $50 for 3 at the nearby Frontier Diner(better than Euro Diner I see mentioned in another review,and a minute away) tho also spent as much as over $300 at Keens Steakhouse which was excellent too...got to push the boat out sometimes.Anyway room was brill and big and ideally suits a family.I see the Hotel has 2 bed Suites which I didnt know.They must be brill.Moving on from accommodation.Price.We paid something slightly over 拢1200 for 7 nights.Think you will find that is value for a very central location and for 3.As someone else said,only 10 min walk from Grand Central for the subway and altho I wouldnt recommend it with young children or 'whatever' teenagers and in Summer it can be hot,one can walk to alot of places.On my last day I walked from the Hotel to the Guggenheim museum (about 89th Street from memory) and which is further up Central Park than the Met Museum,and back.Staff were lovely. I read a review indicating that they were unhelpful.Nothing could be further from the truth.They are extremely friendly and helpful.Just ask whatever at reception and you will find help willingly and expertly given.Want to go on a helicopter trip then reception will refer you to Carlos ,one of the lobby staff.Need a taxi,Patrick from Shannon,Ireland who has been in the USA for 25 years will sort it efficiently and talk to you about football - which he loves (Celtic).(Black Lincoln booked to pick you up at the Hotel at your stated time for JFK is $50 plus $5 toll and whatever tip($10) .So location,accommodation,price and staff covered,hopefully you get the picture.Okay if money is no object you may well do better but for a mid priced hotel,Id be surprised you could do better on all counts elsewhere.Oh and what really did it for me was the adjacent terrace/plaza.The highlight of each day was sat there on my own (daughters watching american telly) take away coffee in hand ....smoking.Pure pleasure!Best takeaway coffee one block up on other side of road.

<Content>Check your bill when you leave! The hotel is generally OK but getting shabby - good for an extended stay as there is a kitchenette, basic but functional and clean. I reported this to the HQ of Affinia who did not bother to acknowledge or reply. Suggest you check your bill for unexpected charges before you leave.

<Author>bglewandowski
<Content>Ouch! Let me say the good things first: spacious room, attentive bellman, great valet parking, location close enough to Grand Central and subways.Okay now for the part I don't like to write about but this stay started off as a complete disaster. We arrived for the 3pm check-in time that the hotel stated. We were told it would be 20 minutes more as the room was not ready. The bellman took our luggage up to the room while we went and sat outside. We checked back 25 -30 minutes later and were told the room still wasn't ready. The front desk person asked housekeeping to call her when it was done. She explained that the previous party had stayed for a late checkout... not sure why we had to suffer though...We checked back bit after 4 pm after sitting outside on the table and chairs next to the abandoned restaurant that once occupied the hotel building. When we went in and asked, the front desk person still hadn't heard about the room. She called housekeeping and they said that they didn't know if it was done and that the front desk should send the bellman to check on it. The bellman was no where to be seen at this point so we had to wait until 4:30 when he went up and gave the okay. We received our key-cards and headed to the room.Arriving in the room we found it to be dated but fairly clean and very spacious with nice city views... room 17 G. However, even though we booked a two queen beds and another queen bed suite, we got a two queen bed with two twin bed suite. We even had Expedia call for us to verify that was what we would get but we didn't end up with it after all. The front desk explained that it can not guarantee a room type even though an Eastgate reservation person had guaranteed this to Expedia. We had to have a portable twin bed brought up so no one had to sleep in the living room.It was at this point we noted that the air conditioning in the twin bed room did not work, so we placed another call to the front desk and they said they would send up maintenance. They arrived within the half-hour and looked at the a/c unit. He determined it was a broken condenser and said the entire unit would be replaced but he had a new one. A short while later he returned with the massive unit and began to do the replacement. We were unable to unpack as this room was the scene of some major construction! About 30 minutes later he determined that the new unit was also bad and decided to try one more unit.The dinner hour was upon us and we were starving... but we had no idea if we would be keeping this room as it was partially un-airconditioned and it was 90 degrees outside. After waiting another 15 minutes or so, I went down to the front desk to discuss the general suckiness of our visit thus far and to speak with a manager. She arrived and her name I believe was Donna. She was very nice and helpful. She said she was willing to move us to another similar suite (2 queens, 2 twins) but it was on the 13th floor which was the smoking floor. We weren't too thrilled by that. She asked us to come see it and smell it with her as she felt most people don't smoke much anymore. We went her and it was nice and did not smell that much and had more up-to-date kitchen appliances.At that point, my cell phone rang... it was my wife and she informed me that the new a/c unit was in and working, so we went with Donna the manager to confirm. It worked great!Unfortunately it was now 7pm which was 4 hours from our scheduled check-in. After unpacking, we got to eat and proceeded on our late evening with the kids who were antsy and cranky now.Things seemed to be progressing... at least until I laid upon the most uncomfortable and squeaky twin bed I had laid upon since my childhood. Fortunately the days events had tired me and I slept well.The next morning, we all showered and tossed our towels on the floors in the bathrooms. We returned from a theatre matinee around 6 pm, ready to shower and go out to dinner at a nearby restaurant. Showers were put on hold because there was not one single towel in our room!So, of course, I called the front desk. They said they would tell housekeeping.30 minutes later, no towels, so I called again. Again they said they would be right up.Another 30 minutes passed as I was about to reach for the phone again, the towels arrived... but there were only 3 of them... for 6 people. I asked the house keeping person why and they told me that they had run out of towels.Weird. They have tons of extra a/c units but lack towels?Well, some of us skipped showers and I went to the front desk on the way to dinner. I told them about how silly the towel situation and they promised more towels.When we returned from dinner, there were stacks of towels in both bathrooms and an extra big stack in the living room. I guess they bought more???Anyway, After that our remaining three days were quiet and went smoothly. 2 of 4 nights/days were just fine.. is 50% okay for a visit that cost nearly $2k? I am not sure yet....

<Author>raven_rt
<Content>Enjoyable Place to Stay We stayed at the Eastgate tower for 7 nights and it was a very good expierance. Location: It is about 5 minutes walk from the UN Embassy, 10 minutes from Grand Central Station and about 20-25 minutes walk from Time Square. We found that most of the places we needed to go to started from Time Square so if you don't want to walk there each day you can take a taxi for around $8 (includes tip) or take one of the many buses that drive buy, which costs a $2 a ride. Room: The furnishings were basic but everything was clean and tidy. We didn't really use the kitchen to cook due to as the New Yorkers say Why cook when you have 36,000 restaurants also it worked out similar in price to eat in as it did to eat out. If you are a light sleeper like me then be warned that in the summer the air con is loud and even if it is switched off you can still hear everyone elses (pair of ear plugs sorted the problem for me).Staff: Really friendly and helpful.Overall I would say to anyone who has the money to get a hotel closer to Time Square, however if you cannot then this is a really good alternative.

<Author>bull4titans
<Content>Nothing fancy but perfect to see the city Took my wife to New York for a suprise birthday weekend in April. My only concern in getting a room in Manhattan at such a relatively great price is that it would not be clean, but I was way off and the place was spotless on the inside. Check in:The lobby was small but nicely decorated. We arrived at the hotel about 10 am and check in was not until 3. The front desk and bell staff was very helpful . They stored our bags while we hit the town and gave us some transportation tips to get around.We got back for check in at about 8 that night and once again, everyone was very friendly and efficient. The room:We booked a studio suite and it was exactly what we needed. It was larger than a normal hotel room anywhere else in the country and had a small kitchenette with table and four chairs. Once again, it was very clean. The furniture and the bathroom were a little outdated, but who cares. We were only in the room to sleep, shower, etc. . We were out spending the money that we saved by staying there. Noise was not a problem at all when the windows were closed.Getting around:We had a really easy time getting around. We did alot of walking but mostly by choice. Grand central station was only a 8-10 minute walk and there is, of course a bagel shop and starbucks on the way. We purchased a $7.50 one day fun pass for the subway and that was well worth it. To keep it simple, you can stay on the green line and be within reasonable walking distance to any major sites and shopping in manhattan.All in all, if you want a clean, convenient , and roomy place to stay but don't want to pay for the Hyatt, then this is a good place. We were very happy with our choice.

<Author>melbat
<Content>Best kept secret on the east side! I was a bit reluctant to stay on the east side of NYC but man did I become enlightened....I don't know that I will ever stay in Times Square again!The Eastgate Tower was originally built in the early 1970's as a high rise apartment building with partial hotel service. This explains the size of the rooms and kitchenettes. Our family (2 adults and 2 teens) had a 1 bedroom suite, equipped with a full kitchen (including a dishwasher) and one and half baths.. The neighborhood (Murray Hill) is safe and residential with several grocery stores in the vicinity. No, the suite isn't posh like you would find at the W Times Square but it is clean, homey, and best of all...away from the crowded insanity that is Times Square. Oh yeah...I almost forgot...all for about $200 and some change a night!There is easy access to the theater district (or anywhere else for that matter) via Grand Central Station, about a 5 minute walk from the hotel. Or you can simply walk (20 minutes to Time Square, 15 to Herald Square)We will absolutely stay there again...and again.

<Author>Beeben
<Content>A great place to stay! We have just returned from a fantastic stay at this hotel. From start to finish we have no complaints about the hotel worth noting. Sure, it could do with a bit of a freshen-up and the lifts were a bit slow but the size of the suite far surpassed my expectations of New York's infamous tiny rooms. We had a magical view from our window in 22C of the Manhattan skyline including a bit of the Empire State Building. Staff and cleanliness faultless-the staff were so obliging loaning us an umbrella and a mobile phone charger (old style US plugs in our room).The location was perfect for us being so close to GCS and far enough away from the madness of Times Square. The locality is heaving with bars and small restaurants. For breakfast we recommend Sarge's and Frontier on 3rd and for dinner nearby Patsy's pizzeria also on 3rd. Tony's sushi just around the corner on 2nd was fab. Two notes of caution. Margarita Murphy's bar on 3rd very near hotel left such a bad taste in our mouths on St. Patrick's Day for overcharging and rudeness ( 15 bucks for 2 beers before a tip!!!) that we passed their door for the remaining 6 nights of our stay. Also the Italian restaurant Il Fagioli (I think)that the hotel recommend as their restaurant is closed wasn't great and rude staff too. The New York rudeness is a myth, it's a fast town and some people are rude everywhere. Last tip-Coney Island-do it! Half hour on subway with Metrocard it's a toal nostalgia trip and the rides are not for the faint-hearted. Even the Wonder Wheel has a kick.Can't wait for our next trip and we will be booking Eastgate again and recommending it to all our friends.

<Author>Enoikos
<Content>Great Value for Money + Hints  Just returned from an 8 days stay in NY and I wish to share with other travellers my opinion for Eastgate Tower Suite Hotel and a few hints and tips for NY. The hotel rooms are spacious and clean. An important aspect for me (given that it was my first visit in NY) was that the neighborhood felt very safe and the location is good (10 mins from Grand Central station). Also the value offered for the rate paid at hotels.com (-20% sale) made it an excellent choice, despite the following minor negative points. Although I had requested a high-floor non-smoking room, we were intially provided a room at fifth floor. The receptionists were friendly but our request for transfer was forgotten twice. When we were finally offered a room in the 13th floor (not high but defenitely better than 5th) we accepted provided that it was non-smoking, only to find out the opposite. Fortunately, the room was not smelly as the stinky corridor leading to it. The air-conditioner is old-type window-mounted, is very noisy and difficult to regulate temperature. The furniture are worn-out, the duvet covers had holes but the linen were clean. Expensive Internet rate.Appart from that, the room was fully equipped with kitchenette, microwave, fridge, toaster, coffee maker, the closets are really big, the matress is comfortable and there is a full-size bathtub. In brief: I would stay there again because of the great value for money.A few hints and tips for hotel neighborhood and NY:- Frontier cafe is 2 blocks away for reasonably priced breakfast (... ask for a cashier machine calculated bill)- Bagels  More in Lexington and 3rd, is also great for breakfast, bagels and rolls with bacon/omellete/cheese- Try Keens Stakehouse (72 W 36th St) for great Sirloin steak, even better than their legendary mutton chop. The environment is fantastic and the ceilings are unique, covered with hundreds churchwared pipes- Try La Bonne Soupe (48 W 55th St) a fantastic and inexpensive French Bistro- Do not miss Balthazar and Lompardis in Soho- MUST buy the 7days metroticket for all Buses and Metro in NY and the New York City Pass for 6 major attractions (Empire state, Museum of Natural History, Metropolitan Museum, Guggenheim, MOMA and Cruise to Statue of Liberty). Even if you don't visit all, you still save money AND Time from queing. Also enjoy discounts in stores and restaurants (e.g. Macy's cellar has great burgers - you get 15% extra discount in Bloomingdales). - Ask always for Visitor discount or get the coupons (-11%) at departments visitor centre. - For major brands in Clearence prices, take the bus for Woodbury's common.- Hop-on Hop-off buses offer the opportunity to visit areas that you may haven't initially planned (e.g. Bronx - Brooklyn etc).- Avoid the horse carriages in Central Park ($34 for 10 minutes short walk) unless you want to take some nice photos.Enjoy your stay, have a frantic time-out ... if you plan to spent much time in the hotel room, you miss the whole point of visiting NY.

<Author>justducks
<Content>Good Value, but a few warnings.... I stayed at the Eastgate Towers with my family during the chilly month of January. When we pulled up to the hotel, it did not look too good and I was worried,but once we checked in, we were pleasantly surprised. It was spacious and clean. I have a few complaints and warnings I wish to give other potential guests. The first is the parking. There is valet parking next to the hotel and it is very expensive at $35.00 per day! To be clear, that is $35.00 + taxes + tip for the valet. There are plenty of parking lots around the area, but because there are so many one-ways, it gets confusing and you may be tempted to just park beside the hotel. Thats what I did and the car came back three days later with a huge scratch on the side. Because it is winter and there is lots of salt everywhere, we did not notice the scratch until later. So beware of the parking beside the Eastgate Towers, it is a rip off and your car will probably come back with some sort of damage! (Note that the hotel offers no discount at all, which is surprising because La Quinta, which is only a few blocks away gives you 50% off your total parking just for staying at the hotel. )The second complaint deals with the reception of the hotel. There is one person at front desk and one or two attendants that stand around and open doors for people. If you have lots of luggage when coming in, the attendant will take your things and follow you up to your room. You will not be asked whether you actually want assistance, or desire to have a strange man follow you to your room, it will just happen. You will then be expected to provide a tip and the end of the encounter. This type of behaviour is quite strange for a budget hotel, so be prepared and have tip money handy. Lastly, regards the service. We went during restaurant week and we could not find one person at the front desk who could actually recommend a restaurant (and not simply read off the Zagat's survey). There is no concierge (i know it is a budget hotel), but a great alternative would have been to provide 5 or 10 minutes of free internet on the computer located in the entrance. Instead, they had some ludicrously expensive fees to surf the net even for a few minutes. So in conclusion, you will be comfortable inside your roomy hotel room at the Eastgate Towers, but do lots and lots of research before heading out, or else it will put a serious ding in your budget in more ways than one.  
<Date>Jan 30, 2008

<Author>JoGam
<Content>Excellent value and location Fantastic value hotel in good location. Booked through Opodo just 2 weeks in advance and travelled with Lastminute.com on Virgin from Heathrow 15 to 24 Jan 08. Virgin were good as usual. Hotel staff, Alex and Doris, very friendly and helpful. Booked 2 Junior Suites but was offered 2-bedroomed suite on arrival - we'd tried to book this in advance but wasn't available and when I contacted the hotel directly (always worth a try - have had some good deals this way) they wanted to charge us $200 extra per night on top of Opodo price, which we refused. So, very surprised to be offered this free of charge on checking in. Very spacious, clean and neat accomodation - completely the opposite to reviews we'd read! 2-bedroomed (plus lounge/sofabed) ideal for up to 6 or family, consisted of one room twin beds and the other a double so decided that as we were two couples this wasn't fair to one of us we reverted back to Junior Suites. They gave us two next door to each other - good value, clean and neat and very big with lounge area for entertaining and small kitchen with everything you'd need to cook a full meal! Only things missing from room were kettle and dressing gowns (but had coffee percolator, microwave, full cooker, fridge/freezer, toaster) - well equipped. Plenty of deli's/cafes for breakfast and bars. Best restaurant in area is Docks (good value), our favourite for many years. But plenty of others within very short walk (10 mins to around 30 restaurants). Lebanese nearby also good. Go to Central Cafe, E42nd opposite Grand Central for good breakfast. Try the 4 loops bus tour for $79 with Grayline or Citysights to use over 48 hours including Empire State or Top of Rock ticket and short Cruise - good value and good way to see NY for first of second visit. Try Gallaghers Steakhouse on W52nd for greats steaks and atmosphere (expensive), Mars 2112 on Broadway for fun lunch, Macy's Cellar Bar/Grill for burger lunch, Nuovo Latino at South Street Sea Port for Cuban style food at good price. Great shopping and bargains everywhere but do allow a full day for Macy's and Bloomingdales and get your 11% discount voucher from the visitor center. In smaller shops don't be afraid to ask for the best price they can do. Been 7 times in three years and looking forward to next visit already.....

<Author>MarkG_1982
<Content>Surpassed all my expectations, a truly excellent hotel. I've arrived back from New York this very day after staying at the Eastgate Tower for 4 nights. I've stayed in New york before and this is by far the best hotel i have found to date.The reason i'm writing this review so quickly is that i noticed the 2 star review below me and the fellow giving the hotel a hard time. After seeing the review's low rating i read it in full and was surprised by everything they were saying! The lobby is too small? What does that matter? Are you sleeping there??For the record their experience was totally different to the one i have just had and it seems that i must have been passing them in the corridor everyday! This is truly a hotel to recommend to friends.NY is notorious for packing in as many hotel rooms into a building as possible, meaning the customer often recieves a dinky room ... After experiencing this previously, one of my main criteria was to book a hotel whos rooms didn't look like a broom cupboard and the Eastgate certainly didn't let me down.The Studio room that we got was absolutely huge compared the other hotels i have stayed at in NY. It had a walk in closet, nice bathroom, a small sectioned kitchen (gas hob/oven, fridge, toaster, microwave, coffee maker) and a large main room and i only booked the basic Studio room (room 2E if anyone is interested).As some other reviewers have said, a agree that the decor was slightly dated although it was kept really clean and house keeping did an excellent job of tidying up every day.The location is between 2nd and 3rd on 39th street, meaning the area and roads are rather quiet. I heard the occasional siren and honk of a horn but nothing that could be considered a nuisance.As for attractions, the Eastgate is slightly further than most, although (unlike the reviewers below me) if you come to NY you expect to walk a distance everyday. Time Square and the Empire state are wel within walking distance taking around 15/20 minutes, although i would say if you come to NY to catch the buses everywhere then get something a little closer.There are loads of places to eat from a nice posh restaurant round the corner to a McDonalds on the corner of 2nd/39th. A 24hr pharmacy is on the otherside of 2nd Avn and a Supermarket is one block north to fill your fridge with cookies and Dr Pepper.The staff are brilliant, everyone i talked to, whether asking directions or getting recommendations for a place to eat, i found to be helpful and friendly ... definately top marks there.Myself and the lady have already said that the next time we come to New York we are staying at the Eastgate, it simply is an excellent hotel to stay at. I would recommend it to anyone who doesn't mind walking an extra 5 minutes to attractions, and if your willing to make the sacrifice you get an oversized room, excellent value for money and a hotel that i will be visiting everytime i return.I hope this review helps :)

<Content>Extremely disappointed Very disappointed with this hotel after reading glowing reviews on this site and having stayed before at Affinia's lovely Dumont. (Quikbook booking gave different rates for each night.) Was told there were no other rooms available until it was discovered that the door to this room did not lock. Was sent to another horrible studio for the night and the next morning given the choice to upgrade to a junior suite. Door to the junior suite failed to lock half the time unless properly jiggled but it was still shocking to come home to a wide open door at 1 a.m. Beds hard as table tops but no bugs. Air conditioning effective. Laundry located in basement next to housekeeping. Many foreign guests seem to be a reflection of nearness to U.N., as are numbers of security personnel with big dogs. Nice scenic walk on First Avenue to UN and Tudor City. Express buses do not stop at 39th street. Don't know if I would stay here again. Would not recommend it to friends without many caveats.Sadly disappointing. Had high expectations which were not met. Probably families staying in larger suites have more modern accommodations. <Author>CaroServigna
<Content>Great place to stay in the city When I booked the room at the Eastgate Tower hotel via Internet I wasn't expecting a lot because of the fair price I got. I figured that with a price like that a hotel in the city would be just a bed and probably a shared bathroom. I was definetively wrong. The rooms are big and comfortable. We got the bed and a private bathroom topped with a walking closet. Ours wasn't a suite, however we got a fully equiped kitchen with plates, glasses, silverware, toaster and even dish washing soap and scrub (take the hint).The hotel is conveniently located in 39th street between 2nd and 3rd avenue (midtown) which gave us the opportunity to walk to the major touristic places of NYC. We hardly ever grabbed a cab. We walked from the hotel to 5th avenue, the Chrysler building, Grand Central Station, Times Square, Broadway, United Nations, and even Central Park. But if we needed a cab, we could grab it right in front of the hotel.The staff is very helpful. We arrived at 4am on a Saturday morning and we were checked in with a smile. The only improvement they would need is in the rooms decoration. They could use some remodeling.I definetively would stay here again, and I recommend it to other travelers.

<Author>Coppercat
<Content>Huge Room! My husband, stepdaughter and I stayed in the Eastgate for one night in January 2008. When we got off the cramped elevator, we fully expected the room to be tiny because the hallway was so compact. Wrong! As soon as we opened the door, we collectively said Wow!. The room was huge, even NOT by NYC standards. I've stayed in hundreds of hotel rooms, including suites, and this one was probaby one of the largest I've ever experienced. There was a big dining room with a family-size table, a huge living room with a sofa, chair and TV, a full kitchen (although small), a large separate bedroom with two queen beds and tons of closet space, and a small bathroom with tub. We could not believe how much space we had. You could easily have 6 or more people staying in there, comfortably (except for sharing the small bathroom). I'm assuming the building used to be apartments.I booked my room through Priceline. I think it was about $165, well below what you would expect to pay for such a big space in NYC. True, the furniture is dated and somewhat worn, but who cares? If they updated everything, you'd have to pay way more. How much time do you spend in the room in NYC anyway? The room was extremely clean and the front desk clerks were very friendly and helpful.The hotel is definitely in a convenient, relatively quiet and safe location - lots of restaurants, shops, businesses, etc. around. It was about a 15-20 minute walk to our Broadway show. We never heard any traffic noise from our room. We felt very safe walking around that area late at night.I would definitely stay at the Eastgate again!

<Author>newreviwer
<Content>excellent value This is the third year in a row that we've stayed at the Eastgate Tower, and we will continue to come back for many years to come. We take various family members to NYC every year in December to see the Christmas lights, and every year, we have a different configuration of family relationships with us necessitating various sleeping arrangements. The Eastgate has worked beautifully every year - they have so many options to choose from, room-wise. One bedrooms, two-bedrooms, studios - whatever your needs, they have a room that fits. For the last two years, we've had our baby with us on the trip, and both times, they've been able to provide a REAL crib (not a flimsy pack and play) for her to sleep in. This year we discovered that they also have high chairs for your room upon request, and they do stroller rental too, if needed. They seem to bend over backward to be family-friendly and accommodating.The hotel is tucked onto a quiet street between two busy avenues - quiet enough, but easy walking distance to the Grand Central subway stop, pharmacies, grocery stores and restaurants. The rooms themselves are HUGE by NYC standards - lots of room for a toddler to play after a long day in the stroller sight-seeing. The kitchenette is particularly useful when traveling with kids, as well. It is true that the place needs a renovation - it's getting a little shabby with scratched and dented furniture and threadbare carpeting, but it is kept immaculately clean by the very friendly housekeeping staff. I did not hesitate to let my two year old play on the floor - it was quite clean.I almost hate to write this review - I kinda want to keep the place a family secret. But the hotel deserves commendation - the staff are so friendly (seems to be the same people working there for three years in a row, so there doesn't seem to be much turn-over), and the price for the location (and for the square footage) is SUCH a bargain that I felt I needed to let others know. This is a true gem if you're taking a family vacation to the city - especially if you have kids!

<Author>DJ139
<Content>Spacious though not luxurious My partner and I spent four nights at the Eastgate Tower at the end of November 2007. He was in New York on business, and I tagged along for fun. We chose the Eastgate because a) it fit into his expense budget and b) it is located within walking distance of his company's Manhattan headquarters.The best thing about the Eastgate: a lavish amount of space at a reasonable price, both exceptional by New York standards. We had a large living/dining room with a tiny kitchen; a bedroom with attached bathroom; a separate powder room; and two closets. This allowed me the luxury of staying up as late as I wanted, reading or watching TV, without disturbing my partner who had to be at work early each morning. We also stocked the refrigerator with breakfast items, so that we could have quick and economical in-room breakfasts.The rooms were not at all luxurious or stylish; it looks like the place hasn't been redecorated since the mid-1980s. It's all a bit dated and worn, but nevertheless spotlessly clean and comfortable. The staff was friendly and efficient; while the service is not up to the standards of a luxury hotel, it is perfectly adequate.The location is a bit out of the way, on the border of Midtown and Murray Hill, but is only a ten or fifteen minute walk to the transportation hub of Grand Central Station. And, being immediately adjacent to the Queens-Midtown Tunnel exit street, we did get our share of honking horns and traffic noise every morning, but it wasn't a problem since we weren't sleeping late.All in all, the Eastgate Tower provided the luxury of space at a bargain price; we would definitely stay here again.

<Author>brokes
<Content>Excellent Hotel I stayed here in October for 5 nights with my partner and father who joined us mid stay. We were very happy with check in which was extremely fast, our room was not ready at the time but we had been given a complimentary upgrade to a 2 bedroom suite so were not concerned. To be fair the room was absolutely huge and was probably bigger than most apartments in New York. The decor was a little dated and lighting not enough in the lounge for the size of the room but it had 2 bathrooms which was really handy and 2 large bedrooms, one with 2 doubles and 1 with another double.The service was fantastic and what I liked was that it seemed like no tip was expected from the staff. Not too common in NY. Location for us was awesome, right in the middle, we were able to walk to most sites but grand central was a couple of blocks away and there are taxi's galore. Unfortunately the restaurant was closed when we were there also but the courtyard was lovely to sit in to relax after exploring New York for the day. Food wise, the italian restaurant just up 2nd Avenue is an absolute gem! We went to Smith and Wollenskys grill for a steak which was also amazing and would highly recommend, expensive but worth it. Deli's galore, Fluffy's is brilliant on 7th Ave close to carnegie hall for a casual normal priced good sandwich and salad and there is a McDonalds just downstairs if you're desperate.I believe that this is an excellent hotel for the money considering its central New York and we thoroughly enjoyed our stay here.

<Author>Magpiesnest
<Content>good value for the money... Stayed at the Eastgate at the end of November / beginning of December. Good location and very big room albeit a little dated. The bed was large and very comfortable. There was a sizeable sitting area for guests / fellow travellers. There was also a smallish bathroom and a basic kitchen.Please note this is not the smartest, most modern hotel in New York but the room was large, warm and comfortable. If you spend a lot of time in your room you are missing the point of visiting New York!!The Hotel was certainly not cheap but was mid-priced and I think good value for money especially if there are a couple of you in each room making a contribution. I鈥檝e stayed in much more expensive NY hotels and they haven鈥檛 been much better.Please note at the moment the Hotel Restaurant is closed as its being updated although there was no sign of activity when we were there. <Author>StellaBlue71
<Content>So very, very happy! I did SO much research online to make sure we found a clean room in a safe place for our first trip to NYC. Due to the staggering hotel prices, I decided to look a bit further away from Times Square, where we would be be attending shows until very late at night. I happened upon Eastgate Towers and read all of the great reviews. To my delight, all the raves are true!ABOUT LOCATION: On the map, it seemed a bit further from Times Square than ideal, but it turned out to be a reasonable distance...only a 20 minute walk (Right onto 3rd, Left onto 42nd until you hit Braodway) Easy walk for any able bodied person... and (in traffic) it IS faster to walk than taxi (save $6-$12). You walk right by the Chrysler Building, Grand Central Station, Public Library and ice skaters in Bryant Park along the way. We even walked back to Eastgate Hotel at 2:30am and never felt at all unsafe. We felt like we lived in NY!THE NEIGHBORHOOD: The Frontier on the corner is a great breakfast spot. They deliver to the rooms for no charge, but we preferred to sit down to eat diner style. It was FAST, affordable and tasty. Never made it there for lunch. McD's on the corner, perfect for a 3am snack! Grocery store around the corner, Dunkin Donuts close by. Lots of other places to eat.... Duke's (Left onto 3rd) had a fun atmosphere. Quiet, safe neighborhood.THE ROOM: We were in a Jr Suite on the 3rd floor directly above the portico. Surprisingly quiet, considering we were so low and close to the main entrance. As everyone has said in the reviews... the rooms are HUGE! Even compared to rooms outside of NY! Very clean, lots of closet space. The decor in our room was not bad at all and did not seem dated to me. It was simple, not posh, but didn't seem worn out or ugly. I liked that the windows opened a bit for air and to let in some city sounds.THE STAFF: All were friendly, helpful and seemed to like their jobs... even when it was busy. We called for an extra blanket and then went to grab breakfast. We were only gone 30 minutes (MAX) and when we came back.. our blanket was there, our room had been fully serviced and the dishes left in the sink were washed! NICE!

<Author>AnthonyMcNamee
<Content>Not luxurious, but really good all the same Four of us spent the last four nights in September in a 2-bedroom suite and I'd give Eastgate Tower the thumbs up.The one precondition the other couple had for an NY hotel room was that it had to be bigger than the average shoebox and in fairness, the suite we got was huge. As other reviewers mention, it is not state of the art by any stretch. Don't get me wrong, it is not rundown and is certainly not uncomfortable...just a little old-fashioned in terms of furnishings.This isn't a hotel you'll be spending any time in apart from in your room. The lobby is small and serves a function to get you to your room as quickly as possible. Safety deposit boxes are available in the lobby too. The onsite restaurant was closed for renovations when we stayed.Nearby, there is a McDonalds, a pharmacy and a cornershop at one end of the street, and a couple of nice breakfast places at the other. Around the corner is a strip of 3 pubs, which all seemed to do a fair enough trade.Grand Central is only a 5 minute walk away (I don't see how anyone could describe it as further away... the entrance you need is more or less at the corner of 3rd and 42nd) and this means everything in the city is only a change of a train away.Fashion Avenue is about 20 minutes away, Times Square a few minutes more than that, and Central Park about 25 minutes (all walking distances).If you're in New York principally to go shopping, this probably isn't the best spot for you, given the long enough hike back and forward from any of the main shopping areas to drop off the bags and start again. But for any other visitor, the Eastgate is excellent value.  
<Date>Oct 5, 2007

<Author>janthefan
<Content>Good solid choice! The Eastgate Tower is a very good choice for anyone travelling on a budget. Actually we paid a fortune for it, on a business trip during the busiest week of the year, but I know that generally the hotel is good value.The reception staff were always cheerful and helpful.The rooms are HUGE. If you're sharing with friends, the 2 bedroom suites might be a good way to save money. I was upgraded to one ... it had 2 double beds, and another room with two single beds. Plus two bathrooms, a ktichen and a huge living room. So you can have your privacy (separate bedroom and bathroom) and meet up in the living room. Tons of storage space too in both bedrooms. I was on the 3rd floor, and there was some street noise in the bedroom facing the street. I wear earplugs, and was fine with it. The other bedroom, facing the back, was much quieter.All that said, I found the hotel totally lacked character - it was, well, your basic hotel. But it was clean, the TV worked, and the location is very good indeed. We were working at the UN, and it was within easy walking distance. For breakfast, we went along the road to the Frontier cafe, and really liked it. A real New York experience. British visitors will love it! Free coffee refills too.All in all, if you haven't been to New York before, and are looking for a good value base for exploring the city, you can't go wrong with the Eastgate Tower.

<Author>Penzgirl
<Content>Extraordinary Eastgate I have nothing but good things to say about the Eastgate. I was traveling with four friends, and when we arrived the desk clerk told us we had been upgraded to a 2-bedroom suite. The suite was huge, with two bathrooms and a sitting area where we gathered with our other friends to drink wine before going out on Friday night. We had a kitchen with a full-size refrigerator and a dishwasher. I am picky about cleanliness and found nothing to complain about. We paid $400 per night, which with taxes amounted to about $125 per person, per night-that's a great deal for a big room in New York in September.Everyone at the front desk was very pleasant and helpful, quickly checking our bags when we arrived early, and letting me use the health club bathroom after I checked out. There is internet access in the front lobby; if you're just printing out a boarding pass it's $3. We really enjoyed the neighborhood. Around the corner from the hotel is a supermarket, convenience store, neighborhood bars, a wine store and inexpensive eateries. It's a little bit of a hike to the nearest subway station, Grand Central, but hey, it's New York, you walk a lot. We had no problems walking to midtown, Central Park, etc.Yes, the furnishings are a bit threadbare. So what? I'd prefer they keep the rates at a reasonable cost. That minor quibble didn't take away from the great experience we had here.

<Content>Excellent Value For Money Have just returned from a 5 night stay in the Eastgate Towers. It was my first visit to New York so location was very important i.e. safe and close to major places of interest. Our room was on the 5th floor and we were never disturbed by traffic. Even late at night we never felt threatened when walking around.My boyfriend used the gym every morning and tells me that it was perfectly adequate and the hotel were flexible about him using it prior to official opening time.Reception staff were helpful and we were allowed to remain in our room past checkout time on our day of departure rather than store our luggage downstairs. The hotel also arranged our car to the airport and this proved to be cheaper than our taxi fair on arrival.Overall, this hotel represented excellent value for money and we would definitely stay there again.

Check-in/Reception guys were bright and engaging (for that read genuinely helpful and polite) and the place itself is ideally situated Midtown for all most tourist walkabouts. If you like a variety of eateries - you're spoiled for choice: Deli's, Diners, Restaurants etc. Would we go back? Yep - no question. Recommended as a value-for-money residence for when you're in NYC! <Content>Woul definately stay again I couldn't believe just how large the rooms were! <Author>NYCFanBelgium
<Content>Good but noisy I stayed here for 6 nights at the promotional rate of 295 + tax per night booked via their website for a junior suite.The junior suite comes with a queen bed, which is a bit on the small side for 2 adults. Rooms are clean and are cleaned daily. Bed linen is changed every 2 days. Bathroom linen changed daily when on floor (like most hotels these days). Large rooms with kitchen, dining area, sofa and TV area, bed and bathroom so this is quite large for NYC standards. Noise isolation can be better (needs updating). The air-conditioning is an older style fan-in-the -wall-set-up so a lot of city and traffic noise comes in through the fan. The fan itself is also very noisy.We rented bicycles. The parking/garage manager did not allow us to store the bikes in the garages (even though they valet park cars and motorcycles in there) so we had to bribe the assistant.So all in all a good stay in regards to the price but the rooms are in need of refurbishing. Let people park their bikes please!I have stayed at the Affinia Dumont before and chose the Eastgate Tower this time (also Affinia group) because it was somewhat cheaper but next time I'll pay extra for the Dumont which is a much cleaner, quieter and overall better hotel.

<Author>OCJoy
<Content>Surprisingly large room The room was much larger than expected for New York with plenty of storage. The kitchenette was great! It had everything - fridge, microwave, toaster, stove, oven, dishes, etc. Bathroom had a large medicine chest for storage, and plenty of towel racks, which were much appreciated. Good water pressure in shower. The AC fan was loud, but it worked. TV was fine. Furniture, walls, etc. not new/modern, but in good condition and clean. There was a slight smoky smell one day in the bathroom -- I think it was coming through a vent from another room -- but it was very slight.The staff was friendly and helpful and the lobby is nice. They couldn't give us a later check-out time, but they did store our luggage in the meantime, and were very quick about getting it back for us and calling a cab. Maid service forgot to replenish the coffee and toiletries, but the front desk quickly solved it both times.The location is good -- not far from Grand Central Terminal, and a lot of good restaurants within a 10 block radius. Our window looked out over 39th street and was big (not like some tiny windows that open onto alleys that I've had before).The only thing we really didn't like was the attached restaurant, Il Sogno. We went there for after-dinner drinks and dessert one night and got possibly the worst, rudest service we've ever had. Plus, the outdoor seating isn't very nice, and it's overpriced. But no problem, there are plenty of other restaurants nearby.

<Author>chicagofamily2
<Content>Great Staff, perfect for families We spent 3 nights at the Eastgate, and were very pleased. The room was actually a mini suite - in that it had a large queen size bed, lots of closet space, small stove, sink, oven, plates, silverware, mini fridge, and microwave. It looks like the hotel was originally an appartment building, and they converted it to a hotel, thus the stove, etc. For our family it was perfect. The room was quite large, and tastefully decorated. This isn't the Hyatt, but it's also not the Hyatt prices. Most impressive were the staff who were very friendly. We took their suggestion of having dinner at Hudson resturant one block away. It was a super meal, reasonably priced. There is also another local eatery on the corner of 3rd and 39th i think, we went there for breakfast every morning, and had much more reasonable prices that anywhere else we had been. You are in a quiet part of town, close to United Nations. A short walk and you can be in Times Sq. To us, it seemed more of a residential area than a tourist area. If you look at the NY map with all the attractions, there aren't many by the hotel, but that was fine with us. The excellent price for the room, and the super staff was what we wanted. We will definately be back again.

<Content>Huge, cheap but shabby Our family of 5 visited NYC for a 3 day weekend. Saturday and Sunday we stayed at the Embassy Suites Hotel down in the financial district. For about $216/night, we got a large bedroom and living room with sleeper sofa, free breakfast, etc. Fantastic deal although kind of an out of the way location. Price more than doubled for Monday night, so we switched to the Eastgate Hotel, more uptown, at 39th and 3rd. We'd booked a one bedroom suite but they gave us a free upgrade to a 2 bedroom. I think we paid about $265 before taxes, etc. We had two bedrooms, two full bathrooms, a full kitchen, dining area and HUGE living room with sleeper sofa. We could have fit about 20 people in this space. It was quite clean but everything very shabby, peeling wallpaper, old furniture, malfunctioning and NOISY window air conditioners, etc. Since we weren't in the hotel much, we didn't really care. Quiet street but a quick walk to Grand Central and subways. Had to pay through the nose to use the computer with internet in the teensy lobby; that was a pain. Would probably go back if we couldn't find a good price at a nicer place.

<Author>Leen46911
<Content>Great Value in NYC We booked the Eastgate Tower based on previous stays at other Affinia hotels in New York, room rate and reviews. We were not disappointed.We took a cab from LaGuardia and once in Manhattan it was an easy drive to the Eastgate. The lobby is very small and can be claustrophobic when it's crowded. We arrived early - around 10:15 am - and though we were initially told our room was not ready, a manager stepped in, changed our room assignment, and we were in. Our room was a Junior Suite, which includes a small but complete kitchen, large sitting area with table  chairs, sofa-bed and armchair, a king-size bed and bath. The room had a large dresser, two nightstands and three(!) closets - plenty of storage for our clothing and luggage. The set-up was great for 2 adults and 2 kids. The bathroom was small and did not have much counter space, but there was storage under the sink and in mirrored cabinets above the sink. The room and furniture were clean and the bed was comfortable. The carpet could use a throrough cleaning, or should be replaced. It always felt somewhat damp. The bathroom wallpaper was pretty tired, but the bathroom was clean with plenty of hot water.We had a 24th floor room overlooking 39th Street, which isn't terribly busy so the room was quiet. There was a huge window, with smaller side windows that open - we had unseasonably cool weather during our stay so it was great to be able to enjoy fresh air.The neighborhood is safe, with small groceries and fast food options nearby. We grabbed coffee each a.m. at the Starbucks on Lexington and 40th and bagels at Bagels  More on 39th  3rd Avenue. There isn't much in the way of restaurants or shopping in the immediate area, so you'll need to venture out for these.The walk to Grand Central was an easy one and we took the subway everywhere. Sites such as the Empire State Building and Times Square were easily walkable, as is shopping on 5th Avenue.If you're traveling with kids and need a cool break in the sightseeing frenzy, visit the St. Vartan's playground on 1st Avenue just a few blocks from the hotel. Our kids loved it and we enjoyed sitting in the shade and relaxing after a full day of walking.The Eastgate Tower isn't fancy, but it's a great value for NYC and was the perfect set-up for our family of four.  
<Date>Jul 8, 2007

<Author>asmittyinca
<Content>Nice stay at Eastgate Tower We stayed in a one bedroom suite for 3 nights (June 29,30  July 1), and had a wonderful time. I was a little nervous about the whole New York thing, having not been there before. I was concerned with safety and cleanliness and found both areas exceeded my expectations. The room is huge with two queen beds in the bedroom and a sleeper sofa in the sitting room and a TV in each area. This was nice as we were traveling with a teenager and he could stay up late and not bother us. It was really nice to be able to spread out and be comfortable. There was a small kitchen which was nice for the refrigerator, coffee maker and microwave, but I don't think it would be to easy to actually prepare a meal there as it is very lightly stocked with dishes etc. This is not a fancy hotel at all, but is clean and very comfortable and the staff was very friendly and helpful. The only thing I might do differently, is choose something a little closer to a subway stop. The closest one is in Grand Central Station and that is about a 20 minute walk away. That doesn't sound like much but when you are out walking, walking, walking as most people in NYC do, it just adds a litte extra on to the day, especially if you are in and out alot during the day. BUT I would not let this stop me from staying in this hotel again. All in all, we had a great time and I would go back again.

<Author>DanielJW
<Content>Fanastic Hotel, Great Staff Both myself and my other half stayed in this hotel mid-february (during the snow) for a long weekend. When booking, we took a bit of a risk going for the Eastgate Towers due to its low cost. However, all of our preconceptions were eliminated as soon as we were greeted by the hotel staff. They are by far the best and most helpful I have ever met! Yes, the hotel decor is a little dated, but functional and comfortable. Then there is the space, and believe me, there's loads of it. We had a one bedroom suite on the 21st floor (D) and it was huge, probably as big if not bigger than some apartments/flats. A lounge/diner with four seat table, sofa bed, 32 inch TV, kitchen with dishwasher, small bathroom and bedroom with two queen beds and 21 inch TV, plus lots of storage. Then there's the view. We had a great view of 39th street facing west bound and a side view of the Empire State. This is by far the best view I've ever had in any of the New York hotels I've stayed in. The hotel is centrally located and only 4 blocks (10 minutes walk) from Grand Central Station, 15 minutes walk to the Empire State and 20 minutes walk to Time Square. Highly recommended!

<Author>mshbnyehud
<Content>A Good Value in New York Mid-Twon If you're looking for a good value in New York, with spacious hotel rooms and attentive staff, this is a great location to consider. The other newer alternatives are so much more expensive. Well located between 2nd  3rd Avenues near Grand Central, and Lexington subway lines, you can get where you need to be from here quickly.The rooms are very large...like having your own apartment, including a very nice sized kitchen. Yes, the decor is dated but my bed was quite comfortable, the room was quiet (I asked for a room at the end of a hallway) and the service is superb. Wi-Fi is $9.95 per day. There's a very serviceable Fitness Room with two stairmasters, one new treadmill, an older model cycling machine and a good weight machine.During my stay, the air conditioner broke down but was quickly and efficiently fixed (although it left an odor of freon for the days thereafter). I decided to live with it. It wasn't terrible. Housekeeping is efficient and very nice.Yes, the bathrooms are tiny and old but the shower was nice, the water was hot, and the bathroom amenities were above average.This hotel is slated for renovation beginning in September, or so the front desk personnel say. Then I expect that, like the other Affinia properties, the price will go up at least $100 per night. Enjoy it now while you can still afford it.

<Author>missmisty
<Content>Great hotel in a good location I just spent 3 nights here on a weekend trip with my boyfriend and it was easily better than most 2 or 3 star hotels I've stayed in. We chose this hotel after reading all the good reviews on TripAdvisor and found an excellent deal on lastminute (拢384 each for 3 nights and non-stop return flights from London.)We stayed in a 1 bed studio suite which was very spacious and clean with en-suite bathroom and a small kitchenette. Clean towels and flannels were provided daily along with some excellent toiletries from Judith Jackson Spa (shower gel, soap, facial soap, shampoo, conditioner, body lotion, mouthwash) so no need to bring your own! The room was much bigger than we needed for our short stay and would be ideal for people staying more than a week. We were on the 17th floor so it was very quiet - no street noise and no noise from other rooms despite there being lots of children in the neighbouring rooms.The location is within easy walking distance from Grand Central station, giving good access to the rest of New York and is also very close to the Chrysler building and the UN. The area felt very safe to walk around at night.Also close by is the Frontier diner where you can get a decent breakfast (they'll also deliver breakfast to your room for no extra charge). But if you fancy more of a treat, try Pershing Square outside Grand Central. The pancakes were amazing and the waffles were huge. Probably a bit pricey by US standards ($12) but a bit cheaper compared to London, given the sheer size of the food.This was our first time in New York and we were surprised at the short opening hours of most shops and attractions at the weekends (10am - 5pm). This meant we struggled to do more than two things a day. I would definitely recommend going to the Top of the Rock at the Rockefeller Center. The views across the city are much better than from the Empire State building even though it is not as high up.New York didn't turn out to be the amazing city that everyone says it is but if I ever visited again, I would choose this hotel.

<Author>PK6
<Content>Good time at Eastgate I took my 12-year old daughter and 13-year old niece to NYC for the weekend. We took the subway from JFK to the hotel which was interesting (only $2 each from JFK to Howard Beach to 42nd Street to Grand Central--5 minute walk from there to the hotel--JFK $5 connection was free that day for some reason). Cab ride would've been a $45 flat rate.Our first experience at the Hotel wasn't good...the front desk personwouldn't provide our room at 1:00 pm as it wasn't ready. The bellman overheard and volunteered to check the room himself. I think he saw that I had planned to have the girls nap (had been up since 4:00 am) right on the lobby couches until the room was ready and smartly offered to get us in. Not sure why the front desk didn't check to see, but it helps to be persistent. Room was already made up and available. Housekeeping was then great with quickly providing extra linens and towels. The room was very large. We had a 1 bed suite ($270 first night, $215 second night). It wasn't really a suite with a door to the bedroom, but it had a sitting area as well as a table with 4 chairs. Kitchen was adequate--just used the refrigerator and freezer. Furniture was a bit worn and dated. Blankets provided for the pull-out couch were filled with holes. Bathroom was tiny and not as clean as it could've been. The hairdryerwas especially dirty, and there were several cracks in the mirror andtile. Bed was comfortable and the room was quiet on the 10th floor. The heat didn't seem to work very well, but we were still comfortable. We didn't spend much time in the hotel, so we weren't that fussy. We felt very safe. I had stayed at the Affinia Dumont also in the Murray Hill neighborhood--which was a much more upscale property but a further walk to Grand Central Station. However, prices there have increased significantly. I was very happy with the room and with our stay at Eastgate. The bellman arranged a town car for us back to JFK for a $50 flat rate. Nice driver; enjoyed much better than a cab ride. Kids loved it!The location of this hotel is great--walked to Grand Central Station,Empire State Building, all the great restaurants on 3rd Avenue, TimesSquare, Bryant Park, and even to Rockefeller Centre. Only took 3 cab rides in 3 days. The Gray Line double-decker bus tours are outstanding. You can get on and off at various parts throughout the city (buy tickets online for a $5 savings). Guides are very entertaining. You can start at Times Square and go from there. The girls loved the city, especially the tour of NBC. Our only regrets were not making it out to the Statue of Liberty and wasting time going up to the top of the Empire State Building--too long of a line and the girls were quickly bored. I recommend this hotel for families with kids. Great neighborhood, close to everything, very safe.

<Author>greyadventurer
<Content>Excellent suite hotel Needed a place for 5 adults in central NY and this place hit the spot. This is a 25 storey, all-suite hotel (meaning all rooms have separate living/lounge area) in the Murray Hill part of town on East 39th st between 2nd + 3rd Avenue. We had a 2 bedroom suite (1 with 2 double beds + 1 with 2 singles) plus a queen size settee pull-out in the lounge. This lounge was 33ft by 14ft plus a separate fully equipped kitchenette at the end. TVs in all the rooms and a bathroom for each bedroom. Taking the recommendation of an earlier Tripadvisor, we went for an upper floor to escape some of the traffic noise, although, because it is between avenues there is much less traffic going past the hotel - something to bear in mind if you're looking at hotels on the busy Avenues in NY.The reception area is small but the staff were very helpful and there is a smart Italian restaurant next door which supplies room service if requested.It's within walking distance of UN building/Grand Central station and there are great places for breakfast such as Snappys or Frontier (eggs bendedict) on 40 th or the Diner on 45st between 2nd + 3rd. They also have room variations to cater for couples etc. Overall a winner!

<Author>rltje
<Content>Perfect hotel for a family Stayed here recently for three days with my wife, two kids and an infant and had a great experience in every aspect.Service:We arrived from with the red eye from Ca so we were at the hotel at 7:00am. Not only did they let us into our room, they upgraded us to a junior suite free of charge. everybody was extra kind and helpful starting with the bell boy through the reception and the room service. every request was answered very quickly and efficiently (extra towels, making the sofabed, crib etc.). Room:we got a junior suite on the 18th floor. The room is huge not just in NY standards. it has a queen bed, and a sleeper sofa that even when open still leaves a huge space for the kids to play around. the kitchen is fully equipped and very helpful with the kids. the bath is a decent size with good pressure from the shower which is not always common in NY. the furniture and design is not philip stark, but everything looks clean and well maintained. The room has a very large window which brings in a lot of light and the view is quite nice (facing north). The room was very quiet.Location:The hotel is locatred on 39th street between 2nd and 3rd avenue. I personally think there are not that many bad locations in NY, and that goes for the eastgate as well. its convenient for getting in and out of the city (very close to the mid town tunnel), 5 minute walk to grand central and all the subway connections, 5-15 minute walk to 5th avenue and rockfellar centre, and the empire state building. 20-25 minute walk to times square and central park. btw - the japanese restaurant adjacent to the hotel has excellent sushi.Since this vacation was planned well in advance, we got all this at a really good price. Also, i will mention that i have stayed recently at the affinia manhattan on business and had a very good experience as well (although i prefer the eastgate location).

<Author>ukwlb
<Content>Good Location, Plenty of Space, Just what we needed Just returned from a week in New York, staying at the Eastgate Tower. Excellent location on 39th and 3rd with easy access to all the sites and Grand Central Station. It felt very safe walking about at night, but we were only 2 blocks from the UN so that might have had something to do with it.We had a one bed apartment and as I travelled with my sister and didn't fancy sharing a bed with her, I slept on the double sofa bed - it was the most comfortable bed too! The room was very spacious, clean and had everything we needed. Definitely recommend having a kitchen so you can do your own thing instead of eating out all the time. There were plenty of order in options locally too.The decor was a bit 80s, but the furnishings weren't that old. View wasn't much but we didn't choose the hotel for its view.Lovely staff, if a bit slow. I had to ask 3 times for my sofa bed to be made up and 3 times for an extra blanket, but we got there in the end. It didn't detract from the stay at all.Would definitely stay here again. Lots of eateries within a block or two. Docks Seafood Bar on 3rd  40th was expensive, but very good. Frontier Restaurant on the fcorner of 39th  3rd was excellent low priced, wide choice - great breakfasts! Also, plenty of mini marts and grocery stores to stock up the kitchen!

<Content>Perfect ! Stayed at this hotel for 1 week in March. I was a bit nervous before I went as I didn't really know what to expect. My husband and 18month old baby were also with me. If you want to be in the heart of the city, I would highly recommend the East Gate. It is not luxurious but has all the facilities.Anne,Steve  Sean. IRELAND

<Author>jancal77
<Content>Great for long stays I was finding it very difficult to get a reasonable rate for any hotel in New York city for the weekend even though it was the middle of winter. I eventually booked a flight/hotel package through Orbitz (word of warning: you are pretty much guaranteed to get a middle seat on the plane!). The Eastgate was great value for money. The room was twice the size of an average New York city hotel and there was a small kitchenette (stove, oven, microwave, sink, toaster, mini fridge). There are a couple of convenience stores near the hotel. The wifi access is not free but cheap ($10 per day). I thought the bathroom was in need of an upgrade and the furnishings in the room are not the best quality, but in general our stay was peaceful and incident free. We arrived off a red eye flight and the staff were very accommodating in finding us a room as quickly as possible. The location of the hotel is not ideal but it is only a few blocks from grand central station and the bus on 34th street takes you right to the Javits convention center (travel time is about 20 minutes to Javits). There were plenty of cabs nearby and we never had a problem getting around. There were a group of students checking out when we arrived, and I think this hotel is popular for groups who are on a budget. I would recommend this hotel for families because it is in a safe area, the rooms are spacious and you have the option of self-catering.

<Author>camknowles
<Content>Stellar Experience! Stayed at the Eastgate Tower Hotel from February 22-25 and it lived up to all the rave reviews. The rooms were a good size, very spacious and more amenities than we really needed. The kitchen came in handy for keeping the beers cold and warming up leftovers. The staff were incredibly helpful and almost too friendly. Anything we needed they were more than happy to help us out, whether it was fixing the running toilet or pointing us in the right direction for a good meal. The toilet did actually run, but when we brought it to the attention of the front desk someone was in our room within minutes to take care of it. Cant beat that!The location was great, and it was nice to be slightly off the beaten path. Great food right around the hotel - really enjoyed the egg sandwiches at the little European cafe on 2nd Ave. Killer pizza just down the street too. Everything was within walking distance. Grand Central was less than a ten minute walk away and from there everything is just a $2 subway ride away. We actually took the trains to the hotel from JFK and did the same on the way out, and for $7 each way it couldnt be beat.Overall, my girlfriend and I were very happy with our stay and wouldnt hesitate to stay in this hotel again.

<Content>Spacious, but not most convenient I am giving this an average because this is NYC, if it were Dallas or Chicago it would be an okay. Very spacious rooms, we stayed at two hotels in NYC and would probably not stay here again. You are 4 blocks from Grand Central which to me was a major detriment.
