<Author>LorelaiLii
<Content>Simply Wonderful Post-Thanksgiving 2006, 3 days. We reserved a queen studio suite (which was plenty of room for what we needed) and were amazed to find that we had been upgraded to what has to be described as a home: a two bedroom, two bath suite with a fully-equipped kitchen, full dining area and large living room. We took full advantage of being in the most exciting city on earth during Holiday time--the tree lighting at Rockefeller Center, ice skating, shopping, and more; and, then we came home to the Affinia Eastgate Tower Suites Hotel. We were always pleasantly greeted by the doorman or front desk staff, and the parking attendant was courteous and efficient (and the parking rates are quite reasonable for NYC). We were delighted by the cleanliness of the property and our suite, nearly miraculous because the housekeeping staff was virtually invisible. Every detail was addressed before we even had to ask. When it was time to leave, we were able to print our boarding passes with the computer in the lobby for a nominal charge. The views are nice, the elevators are quick, and the location is superb! Our stay: Simply wonderful.

<Content>Don't worry about a thing My friend and I and our three daughters (14,16,20) stayed in room 22G (2 bedroom suite) at The Eastgate this half term (21st to 28th October).When we arrived we had dropped off various parties via the Shuttle bus from Newark airport. However the minute we saw our suite we changed our minds. It VASTLY exceeded oue expectations! I snore, so took the smaller bedroom (big!) My girls were more than happy to share the huge lounge sofabed. My friend and her daughter took the bigger bedroom. We had loads of space-and that includes cupboards and hanging space. There were 2 little bathrooms each with a hairdryer (bath AND shower). The little kitchen was much used, and had everything we needed. The available space was fantastic. We enjoyed being together but not confined. Location was great. Sadly my 20 year old's phone went unexplicably missing from her bedside( was using it as an alarm clock ). The verdict remains open on that one. The staff were as helpful as they could be in the circumstances. The view from front and back windows was excellent. The Trend Cafe is a great Deli opposite The Frontier Diner on the corner.Cleanliness was first class -I had to mop a flood in the bathroom and the white towel used did not register one speck of dirt! It was pristine after the mopping up!Everyone was nice and I would recommend this hotel. I had been to NY before but my hotel was not half as good- snooty beyond belief and my face didn't fit, along with crummy accommodation. This was so much better.

<Author>Nonprofit_traveller
<Content>Price and size are right! This is NOT one of NYC's most elegant hotels, but the rooms are spacious, the stafffriendly and helpful, the location is terrific, and the price is more reasonable than most. We just returned from a 3-night stay in a two bedroom suite. This is the second time in the last year that we have rented a 2-bedroom suite at the Eastgate Tower. The living room is huge, each bedroom has its own bathroom, and there is a basic but adequate kitchen, complete with dishes, silverware, dishwasher, stove, microwave, toaster, and full-sized refrigerator. They have wi-fi access in the rooms for $9.95 a day -- it worked well.I was in NYC on business, and shared the two bedroom suite with a work colleague, as it was cheaper than two rooms and you get more space. We shopped for breakfast foods in a great grocery store a block away, and ate a couple of lunches in a terrific American diner on the corner.The furniture is a bit shabby, and the beds could be more comfortable though are tolerable. But everything has been very clean, and the hotel staff very friendly and service-oriented. This hotel won't work for you if you require elegance and a touch of luxury, but if you want some space, clean bathrooms, and a kitchen in a safe neighborhood a short walk from Grand Central, it is a good and economical choice.

<Content>Great location and space We have just returned from a week in New York, where we stayed at the Eastgate Tower Suite hotel. Having stayed in NY before, we were expecting small cramped accomodation. However, we were pleasantly surprised to find that the room (queen sized) was very large and spaceous. <Content>Mixed feelings...... We stayed for 3 nights last week. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Holiday inn type room in great location at relatively great price. Stayed here for 2 days with my wife for a brief New York vacation. The room was fine, but basically kind of old and in need of updating - needs new carpet, etc. This was like staying at an average holiday inn. We got a junior suite because it was only a few dollars more than a regular room, and it was very roomy, especially for New York. The price was great at about 200 per night when other hotels in the area were all well into the 300 and 400+ neighborhood. This place is great if you want an excellent midtown location and you don't plan on spending much time in the room and don't care about a fancy hotel and fancy room, and you want to save some cash. If you want to have a nice luxurious hotel experience, don't stay here, but plan on paying more - a lot more. I gave this 3 stars, because it is a very plain basic place and for that reason, doesn't deserve any more than that. However, if what you want out of your New York trip is to have a decent, though not great, hotel room in a great location at a great price, I highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>City Seasider
<Content>An Excellent Location to explore New York We stayed at the Eastgate Tower between 26 and 30 April 2006, and it was great. Two couples went, and we had one of the big two bedroom/two bathroom suites. It was clean, well equipped and quiet. We were on the 8th floor, so were most likely to get traffic noise if there was any, but the only thing we heard was the local fire engine going about its duties occasionally. The kitchen area, complete with dishwasher, was a real bonus. All the staff were very friendly and helpful, and I would certainly go to the Eastgate again. This was our first time in New York and I had wondered from other reviews of the Eastgate if we were going to be miles away from everything. We wern't. None of us are in our first flush of youth, but we walked almost everywhere safely day and night. Grand Central; Empire State; Times Square; United Nations; Central Park, and Macys were easily reached on foot. We did get a tour bus (well worth it) Downtown and broke the journey to do Brooklyn Bridge, etc. There was a 90 minute wait for the ferry to land on the Statue of Liberty/Ellis Island, so we went on the free Staten Island Ferry which passes close by - a much better option, and the views of Downtown on the way back are stunning. One thing we British are used to at home is easily accessible loos when we are out and about. I had read there were none in New York, but they are there if you look in all the places named above. Eating wasn't a problem, and the Townhouse Diner at 2nd Ave and 38th Street can be highly recommended.The flight to/from Gatwick/Newark was good, and the Supershuttle from the airport was a free tour of New York. As there were four of us we took a taxi back to Newark which cost the same as going by train from Penn Central.We had a splendid short break; the people of New York were friendly and I would certainly go again - and to the Eastgate.  
<Date>May 9, 2006

<Author>DisneyOrBust1
<Content>Good value for a 2 1/2 star hotel Our March 2006 3 night stay at the Eastgate was overall pretty good for a 2 1/2 star. We were a family of 8 and stayed in their 2 bedroom suite. First off, I have to stay at a clean hotel room, especially because we travel with very young kids. Although the rooms are a little outdated, it was clean and cleaned each day. The room attendant even did our dishes. I was happy with the hotel. There was plenty of space. My kids were able to run around like they do at home. The living room and dining room were one room. They even brought us a rollaway bed free of charge. The staff was very friendly. The elevator was a little small...but no problems with serving it's purpose. Shortly after we checked into our room, the lady at the front desk phoned to make sure we were happy with our room. The kitchen was a little small but functional. The airconditioner worked fine. The hotel is off a main road so noise is not too bad. Although, be sure to ask for a room NOT facing the fire station if your are a light sleeper. The hotel is walking distance to many attractions. Just to give you an idea of distance...Our kids are ages 5 and 1...my 5 year old walked everywhere with us. Although this hotel was no Ritz Carlton and can not compare, the Eastgate was clean and a great value. I would stay here again.

<Author>dking2001
<Content>Well located Great Value We stayed here for 4 nights in March 2006. The hotel room was somewhat dated and not luxurious but this is reflected in the price you pay which offers great value for money.We had a twin room (two doubles) with small kitchen area and single bathroom. Room was far larger than other hotels I have stayed in in NY (despite having paid more for others).Hotel was well situated being an easy walk from both Grand Central and the Empire State Building. Also good bus links on 3rd Ave but very busy on weekdays means walking is quicker for short journeys.Neighbourhood was quiet which meant despite only being 2 floors up could sleep through without traffic noise disturbances I have experienced when staying in busier parts of the city. Good selection of restaurants within easy walking distance (Akane Japanese just across from hotel was simple but well priced and good quality). Also great deli / bagel cafe just along road by jct 3rd Ave and 38th Street.I would recommend this hotel to anyone who wants to be close to the main sights in NYC whilst having a peaceful haven to return to for a good nights rest.

This is not a posh hotel by any means, but it is clean, affordable and (unusual in New York) not an overpriced rip=off. <Author>AstridCB
<Content>Excellent Hotel in Excellent Location We have just returned from spending 4 nights at the Eastgate Tower Hotel and would thoroughly recommend it to anyone who is visiting New York and wants a central hotel without paying huge prices. Yes, it's a basic hotel and yes, the lifts leave a lot to be desired (one was not working while we were there and being on the 23rd floor meant a long wait at times), however, it's location (just 5/10 minutes easy walk to Grand Central Station and about 10/15 minutes to the Empire State Building) and the friendliness of the staff make it a hotel I would certainly recommend and stay in again.Our room was large with a kitchen area and wonderful views and there were plenty of bars and restaurants in the near vicinity.

<Author>NJtravelingmom
<Content>Lots of Space...Great, affordable neighborhood Just returned from an overnight stay with my husband in New York City on Nov 19. Availability in New York City this time of year is tight and rates are generally very high. Reserved the Eastgate Tower Suite Hotel on E. 39th Street for $279. We were originally going to stay a few weeks earlier but our son was ill. I spoke to the Front Desk Manager and she agreed to waive the no-show fee if we rebooked (most won't do it). We found the property to be easy to find and located in the great residential neighborhood of Murray Hill. Lots and lots of inexpensive restaurants, bars, delis, true coffee shops where you can get a hamburger for $3.95, grocery stores, etc. We found the staff to be pleasant and professional, the lobby was small but aadequate and the rooms were huge but in need of updating. If you don't mind 1980's furniture and artwork and love the luxury of alot of space in NYC, this might be the place for you. Two beds (they might have even been queen size), 1 and 1/5 bathrooms, lots of closets, a large living room, a full-size dining room table, 2 TVs and a full kitchette. Perfect for a family who wants to eat a few meals in or a group of friends on a shopping spree who need plenty of space. Not very near any of the city attractions but a short cab ride from midtown shopping and times square...quieter too!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Very Comfortable Hotel I spent two and a half weeks at the Eastgate Towers in NYC and found it to be a very comfortable hotel. I had a junior suite which was extremely large, clean and well-appointed: two easy chairs , a large couch (which folds out) , a desk and a dining table. . . a comfortable king bed. . . and a kitchen. It felt as though I was coming home to a little bit more than a hotel room after a hard day's work. Even the TV was a bit larger than the common hotel room television. Housekeeping was very efficient, and the staff was friendly and helpful. Amazingly enough for NYC, the room was absolutely quiet. . .in over two weeks, I heard not a sound from the other rooms or from the street. This is not a luxury hotel, the lobby is small and utilitarian, as are the two elevators. I travel to New York for business at least once a year: I think that for comfort and economy you just can't beat this hotel. I think the junior suite would be particularly good for families. .given its size , the fold-out couch and the kitchen. Great value. I'll be back.

<Author>hollholl
<Content>Spacious, convenient, friendly I stayed at the Eastgate Tower Suites with two of my colleagues for a weeklong business trip recently and was favorably impressed by this hotel. I had booked three junior suites, but because they were short of these rooms they asked whether two of us would like to double up in a two-bedroom suite. After seeing how large it was one of my co-workers and I gladly accepted (we could have easily declined -- there was no pressure from the desk clerk). We had two big bedrooms, a living room, a dining area, and a full kitchen which came in handy for breakfast and storing drinks. The staff was very friendly throughout our stay and helpful with things like directions and storing luggage after we checked out. The location was very nice ... a short walk from many good restaurants, shops, grocery stores (for stocking the fridge) and a movie theater. We had business on Long Island and were pleased that the hotel was located just a couple of blocks from the Queens/Midtown tunnel. The room was cleaned well every day and the hotel was very quiet ... especially since we were on an upper floor and (in our suite) the bedrooms did not share walls with other guest rooms. The hotel has a fitness room which contains the basics, and the rooms are equipped with wireless highspeed Internet access. All in all, we were quite pleased with this hotel and would gladly stay there again.

<Content>HUGE Rooms - Great Value My family and I had planned a trip to Destin Florida - but had a change of plans when Hurricane Dennis decided to join in. We booked a last minute trip to NYC on Expedia. We stayed 6 days at the Eastgate Towers - in a two bedroom suite on the 8th Floor. <Content>Good Value, Clean Room The room was actually a 1 bedroom apartment, with a small full kitchen (stove, fridge, microwave, etc.), bathroom, bedroom (2 Q beds), living room (TV, desk foldout couch/bed), and dining area (seating for 6). The hotel area seemed safe (we were surrounded by what looked like residential towers) and even though we were only a few blocks from 42nd, the area was quiet. It made us feel as if we were living in NYC and not just staying at a hotel. When we return to NYC, we will stay here again.

<Content>Cheapest I Could Find,Which Wasnt That Cheap But A Nice Stay And Great Location! Hotel : Eastgate TowerLocation : New YorkTime Of Stay : April 30-May 1 2005I spent hours searching the internet for a decent place to stay in New York i.e. somewhere with a bed and a shower (not sharing). I found the minimum price to be well over 拢100 because unfortunately the 1st May was the start of the expensive pricing season, and also a Saturday. That in mind, this hotel was the cheapest of the lot (with ok TripAdvisor reviews) at 拢135 or so. It is crazy to think I could have stayed for 3 nights in other places on my trip for the same price but that's New York for you! Anyway, I arrived rather earlier than planned about 12 - the room wasn't supposed to be ready until later, I think 4pm. When I arrived they phoned to check with someone and said 1:30pm, though they had it ready for 12:30 which was great! The room was nicely laid out. There was a corridor with a bathroom coming off it, and then another doorway a bit further down to the kitchen area (oven, microwave, fridge, cutlery). Then you came to the bedroom area which was big and spacious - it had a table and chairs which made it a nice place for having friends over. The local subway station was Grand Central Station which was just a couple of blocks away. The reception and bell people were very helpful and polite. They offered to arrange a taxi for me if needed however I walked to Grand Central Station as it was cheaper and not very far.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Average hotel My boyfriend and I spent 5 nights at the Eastgate in a studio suite. The suite included a small kitchen with sink, microwave, stove, pots, pans, dishes. The bedroom area was larger than most NY rooms I've stayed in but was still smaller than I expected. Although the room was clean, the furniture and carpeting were quite worn. Once again, more worn than I expected. Don't be fooled by the internet photos!! The rooms are nothing spectacular.We stayed on the third floor facing south and had absolutely no problems with street noise. The location is ok but it really depends on what you plan on doing while you're there. If you're planning on using the subway to get around, you're a good 15-20 minute walk to the nearest station, Grand Central. If you're planning on going to see the major attractions, they're mostly quite a distance from the Eastgate. Frankly I see no advantage to staying in the Murray Hill area if you're a tourist. If you only want to visit the UN and stare at the Chrysler building, then it's the place for you. The hotel staff were very friendly and attentive. The restaurant staff (one waiter in particular) was rude and arrogant and I would therefore not recommend eating there or even stopping in for a drink.We paid $111.00/night + room tax through Skyauction and were reasonably satisfied. However, I would not have paid the $180.00/night + that the hotel normally charges.In a nutshell, if you can get a good room rate, there's nothing wrong with the Eastgate. It's an average hotel with average rooms. But for the same price you can stay in Times Square or anywhere in the theatre district, near subway stations.

<Author>gmh8285
<Content>A great find I took my kids to the city for a week long vacation in August. This hotel looks like converted studio apartments and I suspect many of the units are still used as such. This hotel has much to offer for the visitor that is not looking for pampering but wants a good home base while on vacation. No concierge, no doorman, no real lobby, slow elevators. So what. Huge rooms for the price by NYC standards and the kitchenette allowed us to eat one meal a day in saving lots of money. Staff was very friendly and helpful. We were very impressed with the quietness of the room too. I think this is due to the fact that this used to be apartments where this would be more important for tenants than a hotel where people only stay a few days. Whatever the reason, we were pleasantly surprised.Murray Hill was a great neighborhood also. Go to the Frontier diner half a block away for a nice, cheap breakfast (about $20 with tip for the three of us). Many, many restaurants, bagel shops, and grocery stores on 3rd Avenue just south of the hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Eastgate met all high expectations! I've stayed at Eastgate Tower Suite hotel from July 10th until July 24th with my wife for our honeymoon trip. After thorough search (mostly through Tripadvisor), we opted for Eastgate based on reviews, and then location, price and amenities.We've booked a junior suite directly with the hotel even though we could've found a better deal through some other travel agency. I would've used that 'card' if found in a situation to argue the quality of service.Fortunately, it wasn't needed at all. In my reservation I had mentioned that this was a honeymoon trip, that we want to make it as special as possible and that we'd like a non-smoking suite with street view above 5th floor. What we got was beyond any expectation: great suite on 22nd floor with street view (everything is street view from that height which we found especially interesting and NY-ish), path from the door to the bed of rose petals, bed covered with petals and a couple of roses, more petals in the bathroom, couple more roses on the table, a personalized greeting card from the hotel, two small boxes with chocolate candies, a book of love poetry, champagne and, erm, can of whipped cream on a silver tray in the fridge. We were hoping for something extra but this was really nice! Suite was great, very spacious for the two of us, much light from outside and also many lamps inside, furniture in very good shape, comfy bed, all very clean, even the carpet which is usually in poor shape in many hotels. The bathroom was also in an excellent shape and as clean as possible. Everything was functioning properly: AC, TV, phone, microwave, stove, fridge... Closet space was more than enough for a longer stay like ours (for 2 people, anyway...). Towels and sheets were changed daily and cleaning staff was respecting our daily late-leaving. Surrounding didn't seem any dangerous and we didn't mind some walking from and to the hotel (5th Avenue is 5 blocks away, subway at Grand Central station also 5 blocks away, Loews movie theater 7 small blocks downtown @ 2nd and 32nd, several 24hrs convenience stores in the same block, many fine delis all around the neighborhood (we especially liked Food Merchants @ 40th st between Park and Madison for breakfast). Didn't try the resident Sogno restaurant, though...Staff was also exceptionally nice, as expected based on the reviews. As we've had a late flight back to Europe, it was no problem to check-out at 6pm.Any bad things after all this praising? Well, the elevators could be somewhat faster, the lobby is very small, as well as the corridors on the floors. Wood furniture (tables, bedside cabinets, drawer cabinet...) would look finer in dark wood than in ivory-colored combination... These aren't really bad things: if we wanted giant lobby, spacious corridors with armchairs, superquick elevators and mahogany furniture, we'd look for the most expensive hotel in NYC. For all other details, Eatsgate was just as fine. Have we just been fortunate or treated better since it was a honeymoon? I doubt it. I guess that some rooms might be in different shape but I'm sure that a staff this helpful can overcome each issue with a guest. We didn' have any, really.Eastgate Tower has met all our high expectations and we will surely come there again, hopefully already next summer for our 'honeymoon re-run'.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent value and good location. My wife and I spent 6 nights at the Eastgate (16-21 May) and we couldn't fault the hotel. This was our 2nd trip to New York - 1st trip we made the mistake of staying at the Pennsylvania - having learnt our lesson there we knew we would have to pay a bit more to get acceptable accomodation -the Eastgate didn't let us down. We stayed in a one bed suite (13th floor) and it was a real treat to have a kitchen, large lounge, 2 double beds, an en-suite bathroom and a cloakroom. All of the accomodation was extremely clean, well presented and roomy. There is maid service every day and there was little noise from the street.I requested a smoking room and fully expected a smoky aroma with yellow stained walls and ceilings - I was totally amazed that the suite was so clean and without any smell or evidence that it actually was a smoking suite - I had to check with reception that we had been put in the right suite.The staff at the Eastgate all were very friendly and helpful. We didn't try the restaurant on the ground floor as we felt the prices looked a bit steep but there are so many local bars, restaurants  diners that you don't have to look far for a good value meal.Some revieweres have mentioned that the Eastgate is a bit isolated and a lot of walking is needed to get to the main areas of Manhattan - with so many places to visit in the city over such a large area it doesn't matter where you stay you've got a lot of leg work to do......I personally don't mind a bit of walking - helps to burn some off some of the calories.Overall an excellent hotel and we look forward to returning.

<Author>BristolVicki
<Content>Great location for the price My partner and I stayed at the Eastgate over the May day bank holiday weekend. We had got the Eastgate as part of a really good deal on Expedia for 拢350 including flights (with good flight times) for 4 nights. The Eastgate is a lot shabbier than it looks on its pictures and is a little tatty around the edges, but its clean and tidy and has all the basics that you require. Having the kitchenette and a dining table is handy as a couple of nights we were too tired to go out we brought back some takeout and you can keep cold drinks in the fridge. We were on the 5th floor and so did get street noise and the windows dont hold out any noise at all, fortunately though its not a particulary busy street and was usually pretty quiet overnight. A maid came every day and changed our towels, made our bed and did any washing up. The Eastgate is in a great location to get to all the sites on foot or if you prefer by subway as Grand Central Station is within 5 minutes walk. There are plenty of bars, pubs, restaurants, delis and shops nearby. Basically the Eastgate doesnt offer any frills, but offers a clean place to sleep, at a good location for a great price and if you are anything like we were, you spend very little time there anyway.

<Author>PDDNOSMom
<Content>Affordable weekend getaway We stayed overnight on 3/20 to celebrate our aniversary. We checked in, and originally were given a very smoky room, which we asked to change. (I never specified non-smoking when I made the reservations and I wasn't asked if I had a preference - so if you have a preference be sure to state it!) We were then upgraded to a very nice junior suite on the 25th floor, and were not charged the difference. Incidentally, we were also with another couple and the bellman went out of his way to go to their room (which was very nice) to let them know that we had changed rooms! This was above average service in a city where you do not always find this. The only negative comment I would make is that the decor, while nice, isn't quite as luxurious as the website leads you to believe. This was a nice place to stay in NYC and a junior suite is more than adequate if you bring your family with you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Find! I had to be in New York City for a week in the beginning of March. This hotel was absolutely wonderful for the price I paid. The staff was very nice and helpful to me even though I wasn't their regular type of customer, and the room and bathroom were spacious and clean. The location is excellent if you like that Times Square area (I do not, but the Village is just a train-ride away) and I was able to take care of my business without any hitches. As for noise, either I didn't notice any or I'm immune. The tiny kitchen had two different sized pots, one pan, four each of butter knives, spoons, forks, large and small plates, cups, wine glasses, and bowls. There was plenty of storage space and the bed was lovely. I would definitly stay there again. Thanks to the other reviewers as well.I only had two complaints: On my first day there was a smoker lurking somewhere and there was no Cartoon Network channel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>So-so hotel This is a basic 3* hotel in a good location with rooms geared towards the business/long stay market - the room facilities include kitchenette with microwave, fridge, some cutlery, plus wireless LAN available to hire. Most of uptown Manhattan's attractions are within a 15 minute walk.We stayed on the 3rd floor in a room which didn't look out over the road, so no noise problems there.Unfortunately, the walls are very thin - amongst other things, you can hear water running and toilets flushing from the room next door. The room itself was large and spacious, but it did smell a little musty despite being on a non-smoking floor.The staff are very friendly and well informed. As stated in previous reviews, they are happy to arrange a late checkout even when the hotel is full.Overall, not a bad place to stay, but nothing special.

<Content>Top Notch Service I've stayed in many New York hotels within the same star rating and price range and Eastgate Tower is by far the finest. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastico! What a great find! I can only echo the sentiments of everyone else who has posted here. This hotel has it all, great value, great location, and great staff! It seems that half the world were heading to the Eastgate Tower for Valentine's weekend, as that was when my wife and I stayed also. A great weekend was only enhanced by the fact that we had a wonderful room, huge in size, pefectly clean, and with everything you could need on hand. In fact, the staff are so helpful there, that one morning we went out having forgotten to wash up our breakfast dishes. When we returned we found they had been washed and dried up for us! A small thing, but it is the details like this that can really enhance a place's reputation. The location is great also, especially if you are in town for a good old trawl around the shops, an easy walk and you are at 42nd Street, Macy's, etc. Little tip, but if you go to Macy's, go to floor 1  1/2, to the customer centre, tell them you are a tourist intending to shop, and you will be given a card that gives 11% off all goods! Bargain city! Once again, I can only recommend the Eastgate, a great place to stay in NYC!

<Author>aisham
<Content>Loved It, Loved It, Loved It!!! My husband and I stayed at this hotel from February 15-17 and it was fabulous! The staff is extremely friendly and helpful! We stayed in a Junior Suite which included a kitchenette. Inside of the kitchenette there is a stove and oven, a sink including a small bottle of Palmolive dishwashing detergent and dish cloths, a lot of cabinet space which held a small frying pan and a medium sized sauce pan and 4 dinner plates, 4 saucers, 4 coffee cups, 4 drinking glasses and 4 champagne/wine glasses. Inside of the kitchen drawer we found all of the silverware/utensils we needed including 4 forks, 4 teaspoons, 4 knives, 4 tablespoons, a cutting knife, and a can opener which also included a bottle opener. The kitchen held a regular sized garbage can and also had a cutting board. There was also a regular sized refrigerator.In the other room there was a table for two for us to eat at which could also double as a desk. There was plenty of closet (3 closets) space and drawer space. There was a couch directly opposite our King Sized Bed which pulled out to a Queen Sized sofa bed. The room also had a 19 inch color TV and you are given the option of playing Playstation games through the television (for an hourly rate), ordering pay per view movies, and paying to access the jukebox through the television. There are a few interactive features on the television, one of which allows you to view your bill and checkout through the tv.We ordered room service from the restaurant in the hotel and the food is delicious. They specialize in Italian food and we ordered around 8 PM and had our dinner in 15 minutes. There is a menu for room service and for breakfast from a diner nearby. You can get breakfast almost as quickly as the room service dinner when you order. Breakfast was great too! a good tip: When you order breakfast ask them to send you a menu because they have great food! You might want to ask the front desk for menus to nearby restaurants too. One of the places that has great food is Sarge's.The room had great decor and, the bathroom was nice and clean and the hotel provides you with their own conditioner shampoo, mouthwash, body wash, and moisturizer. The soap that they provide smells heavenly. Even better than some of the soaps that I've used at the larger more expensive hotels. It smells like there's Eucalyptus oil in it.My husband and I added a few of the romance specials to our room. The first night we had champagne and chocolate covered strawberries and we had the rose petal turndown. We had asked for this to be in the room upon arrival but there was a slight mixup with the time. I called down to the front desk letting them know what time we would be going out and when we came back rose a trail of rose petals led from the door to the bed, our sheets were turned down, and rose petals were scattered on the bed in the shape of a heart and a long stem red rose with baby's breath and palm was placed in the center of the heart.The staff is very accomodating and helpful. Check-out is at 12 Noon but they are willing to make arrangements if you would like to check out at a later time. We checked out at 2PM.Grand Central Station is within walking distance of the hotel and there are a lot of great stores as well as supermarkets in the area. There are a few liquor stores and banks as well.If you want to stay at a place that will feel like home, try the Eastgate. We will definitely be staying there again. We also would ike to try some of the other Affinia properties.  
<Date>Feb 18, 2004

<Author>Breck_newbie
<Content>Extremely comfortable hotel, excellent for sightseeing We stayed at the Eastgate Towers over Valentine's weekend on our first ever visit to New York and found the hotel to be very comfortable and clean. We were upgraded to a one bedroom suite as soon as we arrived, having originally booked a studio suite, by very friendly and accommodating reception staff. The rooms were huge and very well maintained, with clean sheets and towels provided every day. We too were slightly apprehensive, having heard horrific stories of other NY hotels, but were very pleased with our choice and would recommend it to others. It was excellently located for all sightseeing attractions, shops, restaurants and cafes and we were able to walk to most places. The staff kindly let us store our suitcases all day and pre-booked us a taxi to the airport. Overall this hotel is excellent value for money and a particularly good base for seeing the sights of New York.
